# Comments for Question 4, LLM=GLM-4.5

== Grader: Claude 3.7 Sonnet ==
  * grade_story_1.txt (grade=6.5)
    The story effectively uses the fisherman's net as a metaphor for entangled fears, creating resonant symbolism. The childhood photograph provides emotional context, though its revelation feels somewhat contrived. The theme of confronting fears is clear but lacks originality in execution. While the prose has moments of lyrical strength ("echoes bouncing off ancient walls like a chorus of encouragement"), the emotional journey relies more on telling than showing the character's transformation.

  * grade_story_0.txt (grade=6.0)
    The story establishes thematic resonance between miscommunication and reconciliation, using light patterns as an effective metaphor for understanding. However, it relies too heavily on telling rather than showing emotional states and revelations. The dialogue is sparse and functional rather than revealing. While the conflict and resolution are clear, the story lacks the emotional complexity or surprising insight that would elevate it beyond its somewhat predictable "misunderstood monster" premise.

  * grade_story_10.txt (grade=6.3)
    The story effectively uses the chest as a symbol for confronting one's past, but relies too heavily on direct statements of theme rather than allowing it to emerge through action. The emotional catharsis feels predictable rather than earned. While the central conflict (internal struggle with forgiveness) is clear, the resolution happens too easily, without sufficient struggle or complication to create genuine emotional impact. The writing shows rather than tells in some moments, but often defaults to explicit explanation.

  * grade_story_100.txt (grade=5.2)
    The story creates an intriguing premise about cosmic deception and dream-walking but fails to deliver meaningful impact. The central theme of self-doubt and self-forgiveness emerges too suddenly at the climax without sufficient groundwork. While the writing contains some effective imagery, it relies heavily on telling rather than showing Elara's emotional journey. The ending feels somewhat anticlimactic given the cosmic scale of the supposed conflict, with limited tension throughout.

  * grade_story_101.txt (grade=6.8)
    The story effectively uses the bee pin as a symbol that carries thematic weight, with strong imagery connecting it to the characters' creative purposes. The narrative shows rather than tells the landlord's impact on visitors. However, the emotional stakes remain somewhat abstract, and the conflict (navigating the parade) feels like a device rather than a meaningful challenge that transforms the characters.

  * grade_story_102.txt (grade=6.1)
    The story effectively uses imagery (dust motes, aurora) and symbolism (the key's weight representing responsibility), but lacks emotional depth. While the premise is intriguing, the central conflict remains underdeveloped. The story tells more than it shows, particularly regarding character emotions. The subversion of expectations regarding the key hints at deeper meaning, but the story doesn't fully capitalize on this potential for thematic resonance about courage and destiny.

  * grade_story_103.txt (grade=7.3)

However, the emotional impact is sometimes diluted by telling rather than showing, particularly in how the character's transformation is described rather than experienced. The ending delivers thematic closure but feels somewhat rushed.

  * grade_story_104.txt (grade=7.3)

  * grade_story_105.txt (grade=5.3)
